## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the concentration of reactants, potentially with various orders and mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (mixed first and second order)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate species in sequential reactions)
- Saturation kinetics (non-Michaelis form): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (A + c1) (second-order with saturation)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant changing with time, e.g., photodegradation)
- Half-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (diffusion-limited surface reaction)
- Competitive adsorption rate: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence with no explicit time → classical rate law dA_dt = f(A), suggesting an autonomous ODE
- Linear dependence on A → first-order kinetics, exponential decay/growth of concentration
- Quadratic or higher power of A → higher-order reaction mechanism or bimolecular step
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics with a carrying capacity
- Rational function of A (polynomial/polynomial) → enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanism with saturation
- Explicit time dependence alongside A → non-autonomous kinetics such as time-varying temperature, catalyst deactivation, or photochemical driving
- Negative sign convention → consumption of reactant (dA/dt < 0), positive for product formation
- Sum of exponentials in time → superposition of parallel first-order pathways or consecutive reaction intermediates
- Square root dependence on A → diffusion-controlled or half-order surface reaction kinetics
- Rate approaching zero as A approaches a nonzero constant → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium, expect (A - A_eq) terms

**Candidate 1:** `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*exp(c2*t) + c5*sin(A*c6 + c7)`

Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*exp(c8*t)`
No `A*exp(t)` term. Has `c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*exp(c8*t)` but no A multiplier. Cannot produce `A*exp(ct)`. Setting c0=0 removes A dependence from the exponential-free part, but sin provides A dependence. The exponentials don't multiply A.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `A*c0 + A**c1*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*sin(A*c6 + c7)`
Setting c1=1: `A*c0 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*sin(A*c6+c7)`. Set c0=0, c4=0, c7=0: `A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c5*sin(A*c6)`. Matches GT. ✓
Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*exp(c3*t)*sin(A*c4)`
The sin term has `exp(c3*t)` multiplied. GT's sin term has no t-dependence. Setting c3=0: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c4)`. Matches GT. ✓
Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** `A²*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6+c7)`
Set c0=0, c1=0, c7=0. Then: `c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6)`. GT needs `A*exp(t)` not `exp(t)` alone. The first term `c2*exp(c3*t)` has no A. The second term `c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6)` ≠ `A*exp(t)` for general A. sin(c6*A) ≠ c*A for all A.

**Candidate 9:** `A²*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*sin(c5*(A*c6+c7*t)+c8)`

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(A*c3+c4) + c5*exp(c6*(A*c7+c8*t))`
The exp has both A and t. GT needs `A*exp(t)`. `exp(c6*c8*t + c6*c7*A)` = `exp(c6*c7*A)*exp(c6*c8*t)`. This is `exp(linear_in_A)*exp(linear_in_t)`, not `A*exp(t)`.

**Candidate 11:** `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(A*c3+c4) + c5*log(c6*exp(c7*t)+1)`
Softplus in t, no `A*exp(t)`. Cannot match.
